Who doesn't like going to the zoo? I came here for my biology class field trip. The animals seemed sleepy during the times we visited. They must have stayed up all night partying. I still had fun at the zoo even though we had to complete our worksheet. My favorite part was seeing the penguins and giraffes. They are too cool. The food and drinks here can be pricey, but is expected for a park. Overall this place is fun for both kids and adults.<//Review>

< Text>
Had my wedding here at the end of 2015. Yvette was the best! She was very accommodating during our planning and had great suggestions and recommendations from previous events she hosted. We ended up hiring her assistant Delease for extra help with the set up, and her and her husband were really nice and helpful. The venue is gorgeous, elegant and sexy inside and the large patio is a quirky combination of glamour and "street" that works very nice. Bonus: they have a fully equipped, functional kitchen! Her pricing is competitive, they allow you to bring in your own people for catering or decorations (which saved us money) and my husband and I were both very pleased to have found this place. We would highly recommend this for events and would definitely consider planning future events here again.< /Text>

Expect a long wait time, even with appointment. They're nice, they do good work and they do it fast. Five star work, minus a star for hour+ wait time. We went on a Wednesday afternoon.

2 weeks later update: his is my second experience. My first one went great. I have no complaints aside from the wait time with an appointment ~ hour. My nails turned out exactly how I wanted them.

This second time evens the score to 3 stars. It was very clear my nail technician was uncomfortable doing my dip nails with added tip. There was a lot of other-language and gesturing, people stopping by while I was being worked on to check and another technician that translated near me peeked over occasionally. Let me add that the nails look fine if a little wobbly. Now the cons:

1. In sanding down my nails after initial removal - the technician literally buffed into my cuticles. I bled. It's still sore. As it went on there were a couple of times the sander got painfully close but no blood.
2. The incident was addressed with a couple sincere "sorry"'s but it wasn't cleaned or dabbed or anything. The entire procedure continued. Dip stung. Burned the whole time.
3. I got almond/stiletto shapes and when they used the scissors to trim down they sometimes pushed the scissors too close and was "cutting" into my finger. I politely told them when I feared they'd actually cut through to my flesh.

When I pointed out that it wasn't coming off after I washed my hands repeatedly and one other technician assuring me soap and rubbing would remove it (It didn't) another nice technician brought me a cotton ball with acetone on it.
5. My fake nail - to real nail glue application glued my real - nail to my real - finger/bed.

So overall they look fine, but at what cost?

One great experience (with Jerry, will book with him) and one bad. Three stars.</Review>

<user>114231290387607340411</user><name>Janet Fawcett</name>< time>
1437324465178<//time>
< rating>
5<//rating>
< Review>
My family and I have been using GVO for all of our eyewear needs for over 20 years.  I have a medically-complicated visual history, including severe myopia, astigmatism, and eye disease, which often makes my choice of frames and lenses difficult, since it cannot be based solely on fashion sense, price, or comfort alone.  Every optician who works there, whether owner or employee, is patient, professional, well-informed, courteous, helpful but not pushy, and very happy to share their superior knowledge with me.  They give advice when asked, and make suggestions, where appropriate, and those suggestions do not always support making a more expensive purchase, rather a purchase that is the best one for the particular patient at that time.  In my opinion, their customer service and selection of frames is far superior to those of Lens Crafters and of two different ophthalmologists' offices I have frequented within the last 4 years, which I did only because my health insurance required me to.  In spite of their superior stock and customer service, GVO's prices are consistently considerably lower than those of the other aforementioned providers and every other provider in the Santa Barbara area that I am aware of.  Goleta Valley Optical is really the best by far in every important way, and I give them my unqualified recommendation!<//Review>

<review>AMAZING 20-Minute multimedia theater production featuring one of the world‚Äôs most advanced and lifelike human audio-animatronics! Originally built for the 1964 New York World‚Äôs Fair and duplicated at Disneyland a year later in 1965. Updated in 1975, 2001, and 2009, with new Lincoln audio-animatronic(s) and improved projection effects. One of the greatest theme park theater productions I‚Äôve ever seen... <Time>1476637037939< /Time><text>It's not the most thrilling of attractions at the park,  it it is a classic, allowing you to hear Mr. Lincoln give perhaps one of the most famous speeches in American history. There is no real queue, rather a waiting room. Even if you don't want to sit through Mr. Lincoln I would suggest still checking out the waiting room. It's filled with Disneyland memorabilia dating back to the opening days, and the room is easy to get in and out of, so you're not committing to the attraction if you don't want to see it.< /text><Rate>4< /Rate>< user_name>

< Review>
Somehow Great Moments with Mr. Lincoln became a Disneyland tradition for my family. For years now, it has been the very last thing we do before leaving the park. It's a nice way to unwind and/or doze off after a busy day. It's also a great retreat from the massive crowd on Main Street after a fireworks show. Only a handful of people are ever in this theater...even during peak hours. Watch the corny movie then marvel at the lifelike realism of anamatronic Abe!< /Review>

<Text>This was by far the weirdest and oddest experience before and upon entry. With that said, we didn't even get seated to eat the food. Fiddlers was one of the spots we hadn't checked out the last time so we parked, got out, and as we stood outside stamping our decision at what looked like an outdated setting we were greeted by a man above us weirdly convincing us that this was this best place to eat. He claimed he was the door man and that if we wanted cooked fish we should enter there unless we wanted our fish raw pointing in the direction of the nearby sushi restaurant. He spewed out a lot of other things that I can't remember still convincing us that they had the best food on the strip. When we entered, there were only people sitting at the bar instantly turning around at our entered presence. <Review>Went last weekend about 4:30pm. It was dated, feels 70s/80s, food mediocre. Had the coconut shrimp and coconut calamari steaks - good size pieces and very tasty, but breading only okay (not very coconutty) - but the trio of sauces that came with it were odd tasting or not good - which makes or breaks the food. The veggies on the sides remind me of food plates ftom long ago, not crisp/fresh seeming. Then the half rack of ribs, the meat was very tender/tasty, but it had a weird chunky sauce on it that we didn't care for vs a nice BBQ sauce. The baked potatoes came loaded, but not crispy skins. All in all, middle of the road - but the plates were not cheap and it felt more Coco's or the like, but at double the price.

Also, sitting near the kitchen, heard too much swearing and loud talk of things from the cooks/waiters that we shouldn't have heard. Service okay, but more like a diner. Just not what many reviews make it sound like, so I felt compelled to write. If prices had been lower it wouldn't have been so bad, but too high for the lack of quality reveived. Not sure if they get a lot of locals (bar area busy) or people from boats at the marina, but not worth making a trip if you're local.

I hate to write this type of review, but once I saw so many higher stars, I needed to add our experience so that reviewers see all opinions - and we aren't picky and we both used to work in the service industry years ago. Maybe in year's past it was really good (it's been here a long time), but only okay now??</Review>< Pics>

Lovely upstairs resturant with nautical theme. Has a wheelchair accessible entrance located oh Shelter Island. Found it on a walk while my bother and I were on a visit to Dan Diego. Has a wonderful nautical theme with model boats and fish everywhere. We had dinner there, it was busy but efficient, waiter Tom was very friendly and attentive. There was a piano player there for music background. I had the salmon which was cooked well and so tasty, my brother had steak which he enjoyed  immensely. The sides were also good, didn't have room for desert...  it was a little chilly, so we ate inside, would've lived to have eaten outside on the deck, maybe next time.< /Review>

<user>105429266873887922483< /user><pics>None< /pics><time>1460993220235<//time><text>We read the other reviews and thought, let's try it!  I am glad we did, since we now know where we won't go next time.

My wife and I shared Sea Bass - the "catch of the day."  It was $26.95 and not worth it.  The fish was almost raw in the middle and had no flavor at all.  My garlic mashed potatoes were cold and plopped onto my plate like a scoop of ice cream.  The veggies were OK at best and the clam chowder was also OK.  The bread was not warmed to any appreciable extent.

When one goes to dinner on or near Shelter Island, it is reasonable to expect that the food be better than, for example, the Outback.  But this was NOT the case.  For a place which fancies itself as one which caters to the nautical crowd (with nautical themes all over the place), there were only four fish selections on the menu.  Folks, I didn't go to Fiddler's Green to have a burger.

As my wife and I were driving home, I mentioned to her that Fiddler's Green would not survive in San Francisco, where one simply cannot get a bad meal.  We will NOT be returning.< /text><Rating>1<//Rating></record>

< review>
Visited, at a duck boat conductors suggestion, Fiddler's on the 19th of January for dinner.  I ordered prime rib which was very good except for the dipping sauce that had way too much salt in it.  My wife ordered a medium rare Teriyaki Steak.  When the order came the steak was well done!  The waitress graciously took it back to the cook.  Another steak was brought which was anything but medium rare -- cooked through and through!  The waitress didn't charge us for the steak, but we certainly will not return.  The moral:  Don't take a duck boat conductors suggestion for a good eating restaurant.<//review>

<pictures>None</pictures><review>This restaurant is a local favorite and an iconic sailor local hang out. The food is fantastic, and recently we hired Fiddler's to handle our Annual Awards Dinner catering needs. Here is the letter we wrote, and we meant every word! Best steak in town, and highly recommend them for catering!

1/10/2019
Thank you letter written to Fiddler's Green:
On behalf of Cortez Racing Association‚Äôs Board and the all those who attended the Annual Dinner, we would like to extend to you and your incredible staff a very sincere letter of appreciation. The catering services and experience provided by Fiddler‚Äôs Green for our CRA/PHRF Holiday Awards Dinner at the Portuguese Hall on Tuesday December 11th, 2018 was absolutely outstanding.
I have been throwing events personally and professionally for over 15 years, and when things go bad everyone notices. When things go smoothly, sadly no one seems to notice at all.  Then you have those very rare occasions where the staff is so outstanding that your guests are blown away and provide ongoing commentary. The Fiddler‚Äôs crew provided outstanding and exemplary service and made a positive impact on the success of this banquet.  Each of them did such a fantastic job and for that we are grateful. I had many guests pull me aside and personally share how the onsite servers had gone out of their way to accommodate them, and offer up praise for the perfectly prepared food.  The staff from Fiddler‚Äôs truly cared about making this event a success and cared making our guests happy.
We hope you can pass along our sincerest gratitude to Chef Steve and Rick who we understand prepared all the delicious food, to Jerich, Zack and Ed the food preparation extraordinaires who assisted behind the scene, and to the onsite servers Nicole, Tatum, Cortni, and Bradly for their cheerful demeanor and exceptional onsite service.

Thank you,</review></record>

<rating>2< /rating>< review>
Visited, at a duck boat conductors suggestion, Fiddler's on the 19th of January for dinner.  I ordered prime rib which was very good except for the dipping sauce that had way too much salt in it.  My wife ordered a medium rare Teriyaki Steak.  When the order came the steak was well done!  The waitress graciously took it back to the cook.  Another steak was brought which was anything but medium rare -- cooked through and through!  The waitress didn't charge us for the steak, but we certainly will not return.  The moral:  Don't take a duck boat conductors suggestion for a good eating restaurant.< /review>

< Text>
I ordered the filet mignon for $30 which I elected to get with garlic mash potatoes.  The steak was cooked as ordered though it had a burnt taste to it and was otherwise pretty bland tasting. The carrots of the seasonal vegetables were warm but raw and the zucchini was bitter. The mashed potatoes tasted like they may have had some garlic in them but otherwise were also bland. My wife's vegetables and potatoes were the same and her coconut shrimp had nothing on them that resembled coconut in appearance or flavor, though the shrimp itself was decent. My son's beef kabob also suffered from the burnt taste and was not cooked as requested. $100+ for a rather mediocre approaching bad experience in addition to an unpleasant bathroom environment will have me never returning to this establishment.  The one positive thing I can say about the experience was that the staff was very pleasant.< /Text>

Eh.
Fiddlers Green was the only restaurant opened on Christmas night 2011.  Too bad.  It was awful.  After waiting for 30+ minutes to be seated, we were continued to wait for our server.  Then wait 15 minutes for our drinks.  Then wait another 20 for our salads (mine of which as messed up and had to be redone).  After seeing food pile up under the heat lamps and cooks yelling and bickering with servers my steak  arrived - cold.  So that had to be sent back.  The restaurant was dirty with dust bunnies.  The owner was nice and  made his round to tables.  Also VERY expensive.  Most things average priced at $20+.  Value of food $12.  VERY disappointed.< /text>
